    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1243624110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243624110" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31302406-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587240854p2/31302406.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243624110?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/31302406-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23389731-edda">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302406-lori?shelf=read-fantasy">read-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302406-lori?shelf=read-mythology">read-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302406-lori?shelf=read-classics">read-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302406-lori?shelf=read-epics">read-epics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31302406-lori?shelf=owned-ebook">owned-ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243624110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10260840346989640228">From a literary point of view, most of the tales are told in an interview-like fashion. We have curios characters, King Gylfe disguised as Ganglere asking questions to the asas, and in part two we have Æger asking questions to Brage. Therefore, the myths are presented in a matter-of-factly kind of fashion. You should not expect lavish, Tolkienesque descriptions, it wasn't the literary style of the time.<br/><br/>The <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24658.The_Prose_Edda' title='The Prose Edda by Snorri Sturluson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Prose Edda</a> is much more than a simple collection of myths, it offers insight into the </span>
  <span id="freeText10260840346989640228" style="display:none">From a literary point of view, most of the tales are told in an interview-like fashion. We have curios characters, King Gylfe disguised as Ganglere asking questions to the asas, and in part two we have Æger asking questions to Brage. Therefore, the myths are presented in a matter-of-factly kind of fashion. You should not expect lavish, Tolkienesque descriptions, it wasn't the literary style of the time.<br /><br />The <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24658.The_Prose_Edda" title="The Prose Edda by Snorri Sturluson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Prose Edda</a> is much more than a simple collection of myths, it offers insight into the art of the skalds(norse bards/poets), explaining their styles, metrics and so forth. All of these lessons will help you better understand other Germanic-themed epics like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20650861.The_Nibelungenlied__Classics_" title="The Nibelungenlied (Classics) by Unknown" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nibelungenlied</a>.<br /><br />Finally, we have <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13879.Snorri_Sturluson" title="Snorri Sturluson" rel="nofollow noopener">Snorri Sturluson</a> notes on the chapters. Which offer a bit of historical context to the tales. I was surprised to find that these myths had influences from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12914.The_Aeneid" title="The Aeneid by Virgil" rel="nofollow noopener">The Aeneid</a> and other mythologies.<br /><br />All in all, I am glad that I finally got to read about the Norse myths from a source as close as I can hope for to the original myths. <br /><br />P.S.<br />For the record. I read the book titled <b>
  <i>"Edda (Illustrated)"</i>
</b> kindle edition, ASIN B00NCCEJ6O. Translated by R.B. Anderson.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10260840346989640228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8610974396380426185">If you have an interest in mythology, Scandinavian culture, pre-Christian Indo-European worldview then this is a must read book. If your an Odinist this is a must read book, HOWEVER, the Eddas are not an Odinist bible. Snorri was a Christian who wrote this stuff 200 years after Iceland converted to Christianity. There are obvious Christian influences in the Eddas and there are compelling arguments that some of the Gods in the Eddas were never worshipped by Heathens and put there for entertainmen</span>
  <span id="freeText8610974396380426185" style="display:none">If you have an interest in mythology, Scandinavian culture, pre-Christian Indo-European worldview then this is a must read book. If your an Odinist this is a must read book, HOWEVER, the Eddas are not an Odinist bible. Snorri was a Christian who wrote this stuff 200 years after Iceland converted to Christianity. There are obvious Christian influences in the Eddas and there are compelling arguments that some of the Gods in the Eddas were never worshipped by Heathens and put there for entertainment value by Snorri. That being said Snorri is still argueably the best source for Indo-European religion. You just have to take a lot of it with a grain of salt. The translation itself is entertaining and easy to read. Overall you can't go wrong here. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8978760364835408998">I've been told that most editions of The Edda of Snorri Sturluson (say it out loud, you'll love it) do not contain the 'Skaldskaparmal'. I thought this was the best part, and recommend that you find a copy with it included. It's basically a glossary of poetic terms and forms, breaking down the formal riddle-language into easily comprehensible parts. If you've ever found yourself overwhelmed by the kennings in an Icelandic epic (and who hasn't?), this book will straighten you right out. <br/><br/>Seriously</span>
  <span id="freeText8978760364835408998" style="display:none">I've been told that most editions of The Edda of Snorri Sturluson (say it out loud, you'll love it) do not contain the 'Skaldskaparmal'. I thought this was the best part, and recommend that you find a copy with it included. It's basically a glossary of poetic terms and forms, breaking down the formal riddle-language into easily comprehensible parts. If you've ever found yourself overwhelmed by the kennings in an Icelandic epic (and who hasn't?), this book will straighten you right out. <br /><br />Seriously, amazingly helpful for any study of the northern myths and epics. Very readable, as well. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8978760364835408998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2077800565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2077800565" />
    <a title="Cassandra L. Manna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69961452-cassandra-l-manna"><img alt="Cassandra L. Manna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596828660p2/69961452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2077800565?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassandra L. Manna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassandra L. Manna" href="/user/show/69961452-cassandra-l-manna">Cassandra L. Manna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2077800565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12528637680331293427">It was interesting reading the original written source of the compiled stories of Norse mythology and see how similar the stories have stayed today, and sometimes how they have changed. It is clear that Norse culture learned through a call-and-response discussion and that came through in the way the stories were written: a new learner would ask questions and the more knowledgeable person would answer. Well worth the read!<br/><br/>Rate Procedure:<br/><br/>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ - I loved the book so much I would reread it agai</span>
  <span id="freeText12528637680331293427" style="display:none">It was interesting reading the original written source of the compiled stories of Norse mythology and see how similar the stories have stayed today, and sometimes how they have changed. It is clear that Norse culture learned through a call-and-response discussion and that came through in the way the stories were written: a new learner would ask questions and the more knowledgeable person would answer. Well worth the read!<br /><br />Rate Procedure:<br /><br />⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ - I loved the book so much I would reread it again and would recommend to a friend.<br />⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ - Thoroughly enjoyed the book, could not put it down, would recommend to a friend, but do not need to read again.<br />⭐️⭐️⭐️ - Probably a good book that I enjoyed but there was something about it I did not love (e.g. The writing style, the POV, etc.). I would only recommend to a friend if it was their "type" of book.<br />⭐️⭐️ - A book I have below average feelings for and it would not come with a recommendation from me but I would mention it in conversation if related to the book topic at issue.<br />⭐️ - I finished the book but I hated every second of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12528637680331293427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2576731798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2576731798" />
    <a title="Roger Herrera" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45097034-roger-herrera"><img alt="Roger Herrera" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589473757p2/45097034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2576731798?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roger Herrera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roger Herrera" href="/user/show/45097034-roger-herrera">Roger Herrera</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45097034-roger-herrera?shelf=plays-and-classics">plays-and-classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2576731798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3361094890921644815">I recommend it to whomever whishes to learn about norse mythology from its source. In it there is an account of the Aesir and the Vanir; the war between order and chaos, symbolized each by the gods and their jötunn foes; the adventures of Thor and also of the ever mischievous Loki; a detailed drescription of Asgard and of some of the other Nine Worlds; but also tales of mortal heroes like Sigfrid and Rolf Krake, and more, so much more.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!

    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5bY2a6FB79Zeof2kqC3dr783IdQwlWrUCdzwq2dRGuLdynXaX9/PP0vURGtgOwoUPCs8hpdI1JiOq0ZM2uXFFA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4xthtnFwzjjW6/ijKp8fDJswBDjPIrOd/XpHmYROhKHbZyIHj+7u0cOeQWziici3GCwZamj/DdF6DfF+OfpbVw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

These fascinating entries identify particular deities and giants, as well as the places where they dwell and the varied and wily means by which they forge their existence and battle one another. We meet Thor, one of the most powerful gods, who specializes in killing giants using a hammer made for him by dwarfs, not to mention myriad trolls, ogres, humans and strange animals. We learn of the ongoing struggle between the gods, who create the cosmos, and the jotnar, or giants, who aim to destroy it. In the enchanted world where this mythology takes place, we encounter turbulent rivers, majestic mountains, dense forests, storms, fierce winters, eagles, ravens, salmon and snakes in a landscape closely resembling Scandinavia. Beings travel on ships and on horseback; they eat slaughtered meat and drink mead.\n\nSpanning from the inception of the universe and the birth of human beings to the universe\'s destruction and the mythic future, these sparkling tales of creation and destruction, death and rebirth, gods and heroes will entertain readers and offer insight into the relationship between Scandinavian myth, history,       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13879.Snorri_Sturluson">About Snorri Sturluson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/13879.Snorri_Sturluson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1208866690p3/13879.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/13879.Snorri_Sturluson">Snorri Sturluson
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
202
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12688322543677078911">Snorri Sturluson (also spelled <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17413778.Snorre_Sturlason' title='Snorre Sturlason' rel='nofollow noopener'>Snorre Sturlason</a>) was an Icelandic historian, poet and politician. He was twice elected lawspeaker at the Icelandic parliament, the Althing. He was the author of the Prose Edda or Younger Edda, which consists of Gylfaginning ("the fooling of Gylfi"), a narrative of Norse mythology, the Skáldskaparmál, a book of poetic language, and the Háttatal, a list of verse forms</span>
  <span id="freeText12688322543677078911" style="display:none">Snorri Sturluson (also spelled <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17413778.Snorre_Sturlason" title="Snorre Sturlason" rel="nofollow noopener">Snorre Sturlason</a>) was an Icelandic historian, poet and politician. He was twice elected lawspeaker at the Icelandic parliament, the Althing. He was the author of the Prose Edda or Younger Edda, which consists of Gylfaginning ("the fooling of Gylfi"), a narrative of Norse mythology, the Skáldskaparmál, a book of poetic language, and the Háttatal, a list of verse forms. He was also the author of the Heimskringla, a history of the Norwegian kings that begins with legendary material in Ynglinga saga and moves through to early medieval Scandinavian history. For stylistic and methodological reasons, Snorri is often taken to be the author of Egils saga.<br /><br />.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12688322543677078911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
